### #1  THE BLOODY BARON (The Witcher 3)
  W1  TRANSACTION-CARRIES-EMOTION
      the player starts doing an errand for intel, hating the giver; the grief sneaks in under the instrumental frame. (Don't open with "here's a sad story" — open with a job, let the sadness grow underneath.)
  W2  RUMOR -> HUMAN -> TRAGIC RETURN
      flat tyrant (ambassador's description + thug encounter) -> complex human (the quest) -> the flat tyranny returns for real (thugs take over). The arc weaponizes the player's initial contempt.
  W3  THE MIRROR ANTAGONIST
      the Baron = Geralt (two fathers, blood on hands, both searching for lost family, both capable of anything for them). The villain wants what the hero wants.
  W4  THE ISOLATED LOAD-BEARING CHOICE
      the Whispering Hillock — a major outcome decided in a quest that looks unrelated, its weight hidden at decision-time. (The player's "obvious good" dooms Anna.)
  W5  INTERLEAVE / DORMANCY
      the quest pauses and threads THROUGH other quests, so its resolution feels discovered across the world rather than delivered in a line. The family's fate is entangled with the main plot (and Geralt's own search).
  W6  PEREGRINATION (duration AS emotion)
      the botchling carry is deliberately slow and long so grief is felt "physically" through time and distance — pacing as an emotional instrument, not a cutscene.
  W7  SAME WORDS, OPPOSITE SOUL
      the calm vs kill incantations share an opening line, then diverge — mercy (forgiveness, naming, acceptance) vs morbidity (Blood Unborn). One ritual, two moralities.
  W8  REWARD THE LISTENER
      the violet-hollyhock doll — solvable only if the player remembered an offhand line about Anna's favorite flower. Attention is a mechanic.
  W9  ENVIRONMENTAL CONFIRMATION
      the blood/holes/broken-candlestick in the house retroactively verify the abuse reveal — the space testifies.
  W10 OPTIONAL DEPTH
      Tamara's room advances nothing but deepens everything (+ the foreshadowing doll). Faith that some players will look.
  W11 NO CLEAN WIN
      every ending costs — orphans OR Anna's mind OR the Baron's life; and the thugs win regardless. The player debates the "best" ending forever (Sasko's validation: most players FORGAVE the Baron — proof the ambiguity landed).
  W12 DRAMATIZED EXPOSITION
      the Ciri backstory is a PLAYABLE flashback, not a monologue.
  W13 THE LOCATION BIRTHS THE CHARACTER
      the Baron personifies Velen (war/famine/loss). Character as the soul of a place, "deeply ingrained," not placed on top of it. ===============================================================================

### #2  BEYOND THE BEEF (Fallout: New Vegas)
  W1  ONE NODE, MANY QUESTS
      a single incident (missing son) fans into save/expose/drug/rampage/join/ frame/sacrifice — each a genuinely different quest with different verbs, not reskins. The NV "web."
  W2  THE BRANCH-ROUTER NPC
      Mortimer is a single conversation that forks the whole mission (ally vs refuse). Concentrating the fork in one character keeps a sprawling web legible.
  W3  MULTIPLE KEYS TO ONE DOOR
      kitchen access via social (sponsorship) / deception (keys) / skill (lockpick) — the SAME obstacle solved by whatever build you are. (NV Rule #1 in miniature.)
  W4  THE DISARM CONSTRAINT SHAPES SOLUTIONS
      taking your guns at the door pushes players toward stealth/ chems/fists/social/disguise — level design that BREEDS creative solutions by removing the default.
  W5  THE VILLAIN ROUTE IS FULLY BUILT
      you can JOIN the cannibal plot, cook the victim, frame the father, and the game supports it end-to-end (blood-staging, a framed arrest, a linked revenge quest). Evil is a first-class, fully-authored path, not a fail state.
  W6  DISGUISE + TIMED SET-PIECE
      the 7 PM dinner + WGS-attire disguise + intercom-call-the-waiter is a heist-like timed social-stealth beat — a mini-caper inside the quest.
  W7  THE ENDING IS A BRANCH TOO
      the payout conversation forks caps/Fame/Infamy/political-blockade — the reward is a reputation choice, not fixed loot.
  W8  SELF-CONTAINED SANDBOX
      deliberately walled off from cross-faction repercussions so the designers could go MAXIMAL on internal branching without world-state spaghetti. (A lesson in SCOPING reactivity: isolate the sandbox to afford depth.)
  W9  EMERGENT FRAGILITY AS HONEST COST
      the same density that makes it great makes it bug-prone (kill a guard and Mortimer's speech may never fire). The takeaway isn't "don't branch" — it's "test the state-combinations, and isolate the sandbox so failures stay local."
  W10 DELAYED MICRO-CONSEQUENCE
      telling Ted the truth in the freezer forces a Speech check with Heck much later — small early dialogue choices ripple.
  W11 COMPANION-AS-RESOURCE (grim systemic honesty)
      the sandbox lets you sacrifice a companion as the meal — the systems don't flinch from dark player creativity. ===============================================================================

### #3  THERE STANDS THE GRASS / VAULT 22 (Fallout: New Vegas)
  W1  THE DIRTY ERRAND
      the transaction is compromised before you leave (he sent others to die, hid it) — the moral weight is seeded in the HIRE, not just the destination.
  W2  ENVIRONMENTAL WARNING
      the green tint, the mutant flora, the spraypainted "THE PLANTS KILL" sign — the dungeon tells its own horror story from outside; the space is the exposition.
  W3  QUIET-HORROR PACING
      two empty levels before the monsters — dread built by ABSENCE, then released.
  W4  OPTIONAL DEPTH, RESPECTED
      completable as a pure data-fetch; the Keely arc + moral fork are entirely optional. Players who don't dig still finish; players who do get the soul. (Faith in the curious.)
  W5  THE TWO-SIDED KNOWLEDGE PROBLEM
      destroy the data (safe now, but no one learns and it may recur — Science 70) vs preserve it (useful, but the institution WILL misuse it). Both sides have real teeth; there is no clean answer. The quest's intellectual core.
  W6  THE INSTITUTION-WILL-MISUSE-IT BEAT
      the reason "destroy the data" is arguably RIGHT is that the NCR would weaponize the plants regardless of the danger — anti-institutional distrust made a mechanic.
  W7  MULTI-KEY TRAVERSAL
      elevator (Repair) / cave (item) / stairs (effort) — the dungeon opens to any build.
  W8  THE WITNESS WHO KNOWS
      Keely (a survivor/ghoul) carries the moral truth the employer hides — side with the one who's SEEN it, or the one who PAYS you.
  W9  THE GAME MORALIZES THE LIE, NOT THE KILL
      killing Keely costs no Karma; LYING about her death does. A precise, interesting moral model — deception is the sin, not the act. (Debatable, memorable.)
  W10 UNADVERTISED EXCLUSIVITY
      finishing this can silently lock a companion (Cassidy) and break other quests — choices close doors you didn't know were doors. Consequence you feel later.
  W11 STAGING HAZARD AS TENSION
      the gas-ignition can kill YOU if you misread which door to close — the environment demands attention; the set-piece is lethal if rushed. ===============================================================================

### #4  THE WHISPERING HILLOCK (The Witcher 3)
  W1  THE HIDDEN LOAD
      the choice's TRUE stakes (Anna, the Baron, the whole family payoff) are invisible at decision-time. You think you're deciding "save orphans vs kill a monster"; you're actually deciding whether the Baron's wife lives and he lives. The gap between apparent and real stakes is the entire genius.
  W2  THE OBVIOUS-GOOD TRAP
      "save the children" is the intuitive moral choice — and it triggers the worst family outcome (Anna's death, the Baron's suicide). The game punishes the reflexive good deed with tragedy, forcing the player to feel that good intentions ≠ good outcomes.
  W3  NO CLEAN OPTION
      every path kills someone (orphans OR Anna+Baron; Downwarren dies either way-ish). The player weighs incommensurable lives; there's no "right." (Game8: "both choices have necessary evils; weigh it yourself.")
  W4  ZERO REWARD DIFFERENCE
      identical loot/XP — the choice is stripped of gamey motive so it's PURELY ethical. (A masterstroke: reactivity that refuses to bribe you toward any option.)
  W5  DELAYED, DISPLACED CONSEQUENCE
      the payoff lands quests later, in a DIFFERENT quest (Return to Crookback Bog), so cause and effect are separated by hours — the world feels like it has a memory and a life beyond the immediate scene.
  W6  THE AMBIGUOUS PETITIONER
      the spirit is a monster that killed villagers AND the orphans' only savior — you can't tell if freeing it is mercy or catastrophe (it's both). The quest-giver is morally opaque BY DESIGN.
  W7  ORDER-DEPENDENT REACTIVITY (the loophole)
      the SEQUENCE you tackle quests in changes outcomes — deep, hidden state that rewards system-mastery and replay. (The world runs on real conditions, not a script waiting for you.)
  W8  THE CHOICE GALLOPS AWAY
      freeing the spirit = it possesses a horse and RUNS OFF — a staging image of consequence leaving your control. You set something loose; you can't recall it.
  W9  THE DESCENT
      a flooded tunnel down to a heart in the roots — physical descent to a trapped thing; the staging matches the moral (going UNDER to face a buried truth).
  W10 WORSHIP-OF-THE-MONSTER
      Downwarren worships the Crones (their abusers) — killing the spirit "protects" people who venerate the real evil; the moral field is muddied on every axis. ===============================================================================

### #5  DISCO ELYSIUM (the whole-game quest MODEL + The Tribunal)
  W1  DIALOGUE IS THE GAMEPLAY
      no combat; every conflict is conversation + checks. Proof a great quest needs zero fighting — the tension is social, moral, internal.
  W2  THE INTERNAL PARTY (skills as voices)
      externalize the character's competing impulses as VOICES that argue — the player's own psyche is the "party," and the build changes what you perceive.
  W3  FAILURE-AS-CONTENT
      write the FAILURE branch as richer than success wherever possible; teach the player (by making failure fun) that reloading is the worse experience. Failure = new story.
  W4  RED vs WHITE (permanent vs retryable)
      distinguish one-shot story-altering checks from retryable ones; concentrate the biggest divergences in clearly-flagged permanent moments (the Tribunal).
  W5  IDENTITY-AS-LOOT (Thought Cabinet)
      reward engagement with CHARACTER (ideas, self-concept), not gear — and let some rewards make you WORSE, as characterization. The build is a self-portrait.
  W6  DRESS-FOR-THE-CHECK (transparent soft modifiers)
      let players tilt odds via visible, swappable means (clothing/Thoughts) — agency over probability without save-scumming.
  W7  THE UNAVOIDABLE COLLISION
      some climaxes should be INEVITABLE (the Tribunal happens no matter what); agency lives in HOW you meet it, not whether. Fixed event + variable survival.
  W8  THE ODDS ARE THE INVESTIGATION
      everything you did earlier (who you talked to, what you learned, how you built/dressed) silently stacks the climax's checks — the payoff of paying attention.
  W9  PERCEPTION IS BUILD-GATED
      high skills reveal lines/clues invisible to other builds — replay value + the sense of a world bigger than any one playthrough sees.
  W10 MORALIZED FAILURE, NOT PUNISHED
      failing is embedded in the game's THEME (a failure of a man in a failed world) — failure isn't a slap, it's the subject. ===============================================================================

### #6  THE SUICIDE MISSION + LOYALTY SYSTEM (Mass Effect 2)
  W1  THE WHOLE GAME IS THE WIND-UP
      structure the entire experience as PREPARATION for one finale that reads every prior choice — the side content becomes the point.
  W2  SIDE CONTENT = SURVIVAL
      companion (loyalty) missions are optional in name but load-bearing for the ending — the strongest possible answer to "why do side quests?" (your friends live or die).
  W3  LOYALTY EARNED, FRAGILE, LOSABLE
      trust is a live state you can win AND lose (the Jack/Miranda clash), sometimes with no time to repair — relationships have stakes and upkeep.
  W4  ROLE-ASSIGNMENT AS CHARACTER-KNOWLEDGE
      the finale tests whether you KNOW your people (assign the leader to lead, the tech to the vents) — competence-casting; knowing the cast IS the skill check.
  W5  PERMADEATH WITH DIGNITY
      deaths are permanent, carried into the sequel, and STAGED as the character failing at a specific job — not random; each death is legible and earned by a player choice.
  W6  THE HIDDEN CLOCK
      once your people are kidnapped, wandering KILLS them — urgency enforced by world-state, punishing the player who ignores stated stakes (do zero missions = all crew live).
  W7  THE MATH IS INVISIBLE BUT FAIR
      a real survival formula (averages/thresholds) runs under the hood; the player feels the logic (loyal + right-role = live) without seeing the numbers — systemic, legible consequence.
  W8  THE ROLL CALL
      end by TALLYING the survivors — force the player to face exactly who their preparation saved or doomed. The reckoning is the emotional payoff.
  W9  BEATABLE BY UNDERSTANDING, NOT GRINDING
      you can save everyone with smart assignment even under- prepared, or lose people while "completing" everything — mastery is comprehension, not checklist.
  W10 THE NIGHT BEFORE
      a quiet character beat (romance/farewells) right before the point of no return — calm before the storm makes the stakes land. ===============================================================================

### #7  WHODUNIT? (The Elder Scrolls IV: Oblivion, Dark Brotherhood)
  W1  THE CLOSED BOX
      a sealed location (no exit until done) with a fixed cast — claustrophobic, focused, every variable on one stage. The constraint concentrates the design.
  W2  EASY TO COMPLETE, HARD TO MASTER
      the kill is trivial; the BONUS (no witnesses) is the real game. The challenge is SELF-IMPOSED — the player opts into difficulty for a reward, so mastery is voluntary and satisfying (no forced fail state).
  W3  PLAYER AS PUPPETEER (social manipulation)
      the paranoia gambit lets you turn a group against ITSELF — the marks do your killing. Emergent social systems (disposition -> "X is the killer") produce a player-authored massacre, not a scripted one.
  W4  THE INTELLIGENCE PHASE
      you TALK before you kill — learning personalities, grudges, and schedules IS the gameplay; the murder is the execution of a plan you built from conversation.
  W5  MULTIPLE FULLY-SUPPORTED VERBS
      stealth-isolation / indirect-poison / social-paranoia / brute — each a genuinely different way to play the SAME box. (Multiple solutions, concentrated.)
  W6  ISOLATION-AS-PUZZLE
      the real challenge is SEPARATION — engineering privacy via geography + disposition. Sightlines and who's-where become a spatial-social puzzle.
  W7  DRAMATIC IRONY
      the marks think it's a treasure hunt; you know it's an execution. Every warm conversation plays over that gap — dark comedy + tension from asymmetric knowledge.
  W8  EMERGENT CHAOS
      the AI can spontaneously start killing after the first death — the system produces unscripted situations you must improvise around (a systemic sandbox, not a set script).
  W9  THE INDIRECT KILL (never raise a hand)
      poisoned apples let you murder without an action — the victims kill themselves on your trap. Indirect agency is a distinct, chilling verb.
  W10 CROSS-SYSTEM CONSEQUENCE
      the quest feeds Infamy, which can lock other content — the deed echoes into the wider game's systems. ===============================================================================

### #8  THE IMMERSIVE-SIM QUEST (Kingdom Come: Deliverance)
  W1  GOAL + SIMULATION, NOT BRANCH-MENU
      the quest states an objective and hands you a systemic world; solutions EMERGE (disguise / stealth / bribe-the-guard-with-dice / brute force / secret passage / literacy) rather than being picked from an authored list. Freedom feels discovered, not offered.
  W2  DISGUISE AS MAINTAINED PERFORMANCE
      a disguise isn't a costume toggle — it must be WORN CORRECTLY (helmet on, own clothes off), SUSTAINED (persuasion checks, no caught crimes), and in the monastery, LIVED (attend prayers on time, keep the schedule). Cover is an ongoing discipline.
  W3  THE DISGUISE COSTS YOU (surrender the kit)
      entering the monastery strips your entire inventory and power — the vow ("poverty") is mechanical. A disguise that costs you something real raises the stakes.
  W4  QUEST GATED BEHIND A LIFE SKILL
      you can't enter without LITERACY — a competence earned in the open world. Progression depends on who your character has BECOME, not just quest flags.
  W5  CROSS-QUEST REACTIVITY
      infiltrating the bandits in a PRIOR quest changes THIS quest's difficulty; the monastery arc weaves six side quests. The world remembers and threads quests together.
  W6  DENSITY AS OBSTACLE
      the camp is so crowded that rote stealth-assassination fails — the environment's population forces PATIENCE and opportunism over exploit. The world's texture is the challenge.
  W7  FORCE IS A VALID ROUTE (with a cost)
      you can brute-force the camp or bail the monastery arc by murder-and-flee — the elegant path is optional; the sim supports the blunt one (with lost rewards).
  W8  THE APPROACH IS A MORAL STANCE
      "mercy or annihilation" for the bandits; capture-vs-kill Pious — HOW you solve it is WHO you are, and the game frames it that way.
  W9  DIEGETIC SOCIAL SOLUTIONS
      get the guardian drunk on dice to isolate the mark — a social problem solved through a WORLD ACTIVITY (gambling), not a dialogue check. Systems double as tools.
  W10 REWARD FOR DOING IT RIGHT
      kill Pious OUTSIDE and you miss the "strange die"; the clean method yields a hidden reward — the sim quietly rewards precision/patience.
  W11 THE HONEST FLAW (anti-pattern)
      systemic stealth with INCONSISTENT detection ("seen through walls") turns emergent freedom into unfair failure — LEGIBLE rules are the price of systemic ambition. ===============================================================================

### #9  DREAM ON / THE PERALEZ ARC (Cyberpunk 2077)
  W1  THE UNCANNY TELL IN BEHAVIOR
      the couple's TOO-PERFECT harmony (never bickering) unnerves the player before any reveal — the horror is seeded in CHARACTER BEHAVIOR, not a jump scare.
  W2  THE MUNDANE HOOK -> COSMIC DREAD
      opens as a routine break-in investigation, escalates to mind- editing conspiracy — the ordinary frame makes the reveal land harder (see also Vault 22's dirty errand, Questbook 03).
  W3  THE SPACE AS PUZZLE-TEXT
      you SCAN an apartment to read a truth its own owners can't perceive — investigation as reading an environment (ties Obra Dinn / Witcher senses).
  W4  EPISTEMIC HORROR (you can't trust reality)
      the victims' own MEMORIES are manufactured — the dread isn't a monster, it's the impossibility of certainty. The scariest thing is edited reality.
  W5  THE INVESTIGATOR IS IMPLICATED
      staying silent makes YOU complicit; telling may endanger them AND changes nothing. There's no clean hands — the player is drawn into the moral trap.
  W6  WITHHELD CLOSURE AS THEME (form = content)
      the unresolved ending ENACTS the powerlessness the quest is about; you leave with the same uncertainty the victims live in. (Dev-confirmed intent.)
  W7  THE CHOICE THAT "DOESN'T MATTER" — AND THAT'S THE POINT
      mechanically the fork changes little (you're blocked either way; the plot continues) — but it forces the player to DECIDE what they believe is right with no feedback, which is more unsettling than a consequential choice.
  W8  A SLICE OF A LARGER FICTION
      the world CONTINUES beyond V's involvement — you glimpse a piece of something bigger that doesn't revolve around you. The world feels vast and indifferent.
  W9  POWER ABOVE YOUR PAY-GRADE
      the cloaked AV, the rogue-AI implication — the antagonist is out of reach, unbeatable at your level; you can witness but not defeat it. Dread from asymmetry.
  W10 DELAYED, ORGANIC TRIGGER
      the quest calls you later, mid-other-content — it surfaces like a real development, not a menu item, making the world feel alive. ===============================================================================

### #10  "I KNOW YOU" / THE STRANGE MAN (Red Dead Redemption)
  W1  THE FIGURE WHO KNOWS YOU
      an NPC who possesses the player's HISTORY (reads the save/choices) and reflects it back — instantly uncanny, instantly personal. Knowledge-as-intimacy = dread + weight.
  W2  KARMA SYSTEM WITH A FACE
      personify the game's morality/reactivity as a CHARACTER who tests and comments — turns an invisible stat into a haunting relationship.
  W3  MORAL TESTS WITH NO MECHANICAL STAKE
      the errands give no loot/branch — they exist ONLY to mirror the player's instincts. A choice stripped of reward is a pure measure of character (cf. Whispering Hillock's zero-reward fork, Questbook 04).
  W4  THE MIRROR STAGING
      he appears BEHIND you in a mirror — literal reflection; and VANISHES from photographs — he can't be captured/recorded, only lived. Staging that says "this is you / this is fate," wordlessly.
  W5  BEYOND YOUR VIOLENCE
      the jammed gun / the shots that do nothing — the player's default verb (kill) FAILS on him. An antagonist you cannot resolve with force reframes the whole encounter as spiritual.
  W6  "MANY HAVE"
      a single line that reframes the figure as ancient, universal, above the player — one perfect line does more than a lore dump. (Economy of mystery.)
  W7  DELIBERATE, MEANINGFUL UNSOLVABILITY
      never explained, ALL readings supported — the player projects their own interpretation; the ambiguity is participatory AND thematically anchored (he's the moral core, so the mystery MEANS something).
  W8  FORESHADOW-IN-HINDSIGHT
      he admires the spot where John will be buried — a line that only lands LATER; the quest plays differently in memory than in the moment.
  W9  THE HAUNTED SPACE
      the shack (skulls, incomplete painting, vanishing notes) tells his story environmentally and reinforces the death-motif without exposition.
  W10 RECURRING ACROSS THE SAGA
      he threads two games — a figure who persists across the whole arc, accreting weight each appearance (a through-line character, not a one-off). ===============================================================================

### #11  ANJU & KAFEI / "ANJU'S ANGUISH" (The Legend of Zelda: Majora's Mask)
  W1  NPCs ON REAL SCHEDULES
      Anju, Kafei, the Postman, Sakon, Madame Aroma all live fixed timetables; the town is a CLOCKWORK the player reads and threads. The world runs WITHOUT you — you slot into it.
  W2  THE QUEST CAN BE FAILED BY TIME
      miss a window and the chain breaks / Anju flees. Real stakes from time-management — the deadline is teeth, not decoration.
  W3  THE PLAYER AS SECRET GO-BETWEEN
      you carry letters/tokens between two people who can't meet — a structure of DEVOTION-BY-PROXY; you're the thread connecting them, which makes the reunion YOURS too.
  W4  KNOWLEDGE IS THE PROGRESSION (loop-mastery)
      you learn the schedule on one cycle and execute it on the next — the time-loop turns FORE-KNOWLEDGE into the core skill. Replaying with knowledge is the intended play, not a failure.
  W5  THE APOCALYPTIC DEADLINE AS EMOTION
      the reunion lands BECAUSE the moon is falling — devotion in the face of certain doom. The countdown clock is an emotional instrument (cf. the Baron's "peregrination" — time weaponized for feeling, Questbook 01).
  W6  TWO PERSPECTIVES, ONE STORY
      you experience Anju's side (waiting, hoping) and Kafei's side (ashamed, hunting the thief) separately, then converge them — dramatic irony + a reunion the PLAYER engineered.
  W7  THE INTERLOCKING DEPENDENCY (don't stop the thief!)
      a counterintuitive rule — you must NOT stop Sakon's robbery early, or a later beat breaks. Events are interdependent; "helping" at the wrong time breaks the chain (cf. Whispering Hillock's obvious-good trap, Questbook 04).
  W8  MUNDANE TOOLS, PRECISE USE
      masks/keys/letters used at exact times/places — the puzzle is SEQUENCING known tools against a schedule, not finding new ones. Mastery is timing, not inventory.
  W9  THE OPTIONAL REWARD FORK
      one errand (the Special Delivery) yields two mutually-exclusive rewards — a small choice with real exclusivity inside a tightly-scripted quest.
  W10 THE EARNED CUTSCENE
      the reunion is a long, tender payoff GATED behind flawless execution across 72 hours — the emotional climax is EARNED by mastery, so it lands like an achievement AND a story beat. ===============================================================================

### #12  "WHAT CAN CHANGE THE NATURE OF A MAN?" (Planescape: Torment)
  W1  ONE QUESTION, WHOLE GAME
      a single thematic question ("what can change the nature of a man?") posed in the opening, echoed by NPCs, and demanded by the finale — every quest is an ANSWER. The game has a SPINE of meaning, not just a plot.
  W2  QUESTS AS CASE STUDIES
      each major quest interrogates the theme from a different angle (belief, regret, love, immortality's cost) — the side content DEEPENS THE QUESTION rather than diluting it.
  W3  MEMORY AS IDENTITY (the past walks the world)
      your prior selves' choices are physically present — confronting them is confronting whether you're bound by who you were. The past is a place you visit.
  W4  SELF-KNOWLEDGE AS PROGRESSION
      raising mental stats unlocks MEMORIES + dialogue — you "level up" by understanding yourself; remembering can grant power OR force you to own an atrocity.
  W5  DIALOGUE IS THE GAME
      ~800k words, combat mostly optional — the gameplay is conversation and moral positioning; you can talk through almost anything (cf. Disco Elysium, Questbook 05 — Planescape is its ancestor).
  W6  THE GENUINELY-DEBATED QUESTION
      multiple in-world answers (Ravel's "what matters is that you change"; the boss's "nothing can"; the player's "belief can") — the theme is a real argument, not a lecture; YOU resolve it.
  W7  THE FINAL BOSS IS AN ARGUMENT
      the climax is a DEBATE you can win with words by proving you've changed — the antagonist embodies the DENIAL of the theme (a thesis-villain). Beaten by meaning, not force (cf. our "beaten by knowing," Q050).
  W8  THE THESIS-ANTAGONIST IS YOURSELF
      the final boss is the Nameless One's own discarded mortality — the enemy is a PART OF YOU that you must reintegrate. The ultimate mirror-antagonist (cf. the Baron = Geralt, Questbook 01; taken to its limit).
  W9  REGRET AS THE ANSWER (change costs)
      the canonical resolution — you change by REGRETTING past harm and CHOOSING TO BEAR its cost (giving up immortality, accepting death). Change is proven by accepting consequence, not escaping it. (Directly rhymes with our "consequence across time.")
  W10 THE BURIED CLIMAX
      Ravel's thematic answer is easy to miss inside a puzzle-conversation — the deepest meaning rewards the player who ENGAGES rather than skims. Faith in the attentive. ===============================================================================

### #13  THE SUBSTORY MODEL (Yakuza / Like a Dragon)
  W1  SIDE CONTENT AS SENSE-OF-PLACE
      substories exist to make the CITY feel alive, not to pad a checklist — every corner has an authored story; density makes a small map feel vast.
  W2  TONAL JUXTAPOSITION AS A FEATURE
      deliberately swing from grim main-story to absurd side-story and back — the contrast makes BOTH hit harder (the comedy relieves, the drama deepens). Revel in it.
  W3  THE DEADPAN ANCHOR
      a SERIOUS protagonist playing absurdity dead-straight is the comedy engine — and his sincerity lets the heartfelt beats land too. The straight man is the key.
  W4  ABSURD WITH HEART (never JUST a gag)
      even the silliest substory has a real human core (confidence, loneliness, pride) — the joke is the wrapper, the heart is the gift. Commit to the bit AND the soul.
  W5  COMMITMENT TO THE BIT
      build a full BOSS FIGHT / minigame / arc around a joke premise — the absurdity is taken as seriously (mechanically) as the drama. Half-committed comedy dies.
  W6  THE CHANCE ENCOUNTER (the city snags you)
      substories start by WALKING PAST something, not from a menu — the world reaches out and grabs you; discovery feels organic, not administrative.
  W7  THE BLINDSIDE (mundane -> devastating)
      a "sleeper" side quest that starts light and earns real emotional weight through contrast — the setup's lightness makes the drop land (cf. Disco/RDR).
  W8  MINIGAME-AS-STORY
      wrap a character arc around a mechanic (a failing club, a lonely idol) — systems deliver story; the minigame IS the emotional throughline.
  W9  ABSURDITY FROM THE GAME'S OWN MECHANICS
      parody your OWN systems (random encounters -> "catch the thugs Pokemon-style") — self-aware comedy that's native to the game.
  W10 COMEDY AS A DELIVERY SYSTEM FOR IDEAS
      ride a silly premise into a real theme (the manipulative AI, the confidence lesson) — humor lowers the guard, then lands the point. ===============================================================================

### #14  LADY BOYLE'S LAST PARTY (Dishonored)
  W1  THE SANDBOX SPACE
      a whole mansion + grounds you move through FREELY, blending with guests — the open structure lets you author a plan (deduce, seduce, sneak, slaughter). Freedom breeds the fun.
  W2  RANDOMIZED TARGET = REAL DEDUCTION
      which sister is the target is shuffled per run, so you must actually INVESTIGATE, not memorize — the mystery is genuine and replayable.
  W3  SOCIAL DEDUCTION VIA DIEGETIC MEANS
      identify the target by GOSSIP, DRINKS, DIARIES, personality- reading flirts — the investigation happens through the party's social fabric, not a quest-log clue.
  W4  MULTIPLE KEYS TO THE ANSWER
      gossip / Miss White / diaries / Brisby / personality-checks all lead to the target — many diegetic paths to the same knowledge (cf. NV Rule #1, Questbook 02/03).
  W5  THE SPACE FIGHTS BACK
      kill in plain sight and the Overseers' music boxes NULLIFY your magic — the environment has counters to the crude approach, nudging elegance. Systemic pushback.
  W6  NON-LETHAL ISN'T CLEAN (the moral masterstroke)
      the "spare" option (hand her to her stalker) is arguably MORE monstrous than killing — the game DENIES the player a clean-conscience easy-out and forces them to own the grey. "Non-lethal doesn't mean merciful."
  W7  THE CHAOS SYSTEM (HOW echoes)
      a meter tracking death/disorder changes the WORLD and ending — your method has systemic, world-wide consequences (more Weepers, grimmer city). Play-style = world-state.
  W8  THE CRUDE SHORTCUT IS ALLOWED (and judged)
      you CAN murder everyone and win by elimination — the sim permits the brute path but quietly costs you via chaos. Freedom includes the ugly option.
  W9  PERSONALITY AS THE PUZZLE
      each sister rejects your drink in a character-specific line; reading WHO they are IS how you solve it — characterization doubles as the deduction mechanic.
  W10 THE ELEGANT PATH IS RICHER
      designer intent — the subdued methods are "so much more involved and exciting long-term" than the grenade; the game REWARDS subtlety with a better experience, not just a better score. ===============================================================================

### #15  ESCAPE FROM FORT JOY + THE SURFACE SYSTEM (Divinity: Original Sin 2)
  W1  GOAL + SYSTEMIC WORLD (many full paths)
      one objective (escape), FIVE authored questlines + lateral tricks, each a real mini-story reaching the same exit — the player picks the path they ARE. (The purest "multiple solutions" in the canon — cf. NV Rule #1, Questbook 02/03, made spatial.)
  W2  THE ENVIRONMENT IS THE TOOLSET
      the elemental surface system means solutions EMERGE from physics/ chemistry, not a fixed ability menu — creativity "the devs never intended." The sim is the fun.
  W3  EARNED ITEMS AS UNIVERSAL KEYS
      the Teleport Gloves solve traversal, combat, and puzzles all game — a single earned tool with broad, creative reuse (reward that keeps GIVING).
  W4  QUESTS INTERLOCK
      Path 4's key needs Path 1's gloves; Path 3 intersects a companion quest (Sebille/ Stingtail) — the questlines WEAVE, so exploring one enriches others (the world is a mesh, not silos).
  W5  THE BETRAYAL THAT ARMS YOU
      Gawin betrays you, but you keep the gloves — a story turn that HANDS you the tool that trivializes the obstacle. Betrayal as a systemic gift.
  W6  GET-CAUGHT-ON-PURPOSE (lateral thinking)
      letting yourself be captured is a SHORTCUT (prison is beneath the exits) — the sim rewards thinking sideways; failure-states become routes.
  W7  THE OBSERVANT ARE REWARDED
      hidden hatches/buttons/caves found via high WITS or exploration — the space hides solutions for the curious (cf. optional depth, Questbook 03).
  W8  EVEN THE EXIT HAS MULTIPLE KEYS
      the final sewer gate opens by KILLING Kniles OR BARTERING (Atusa's Leg) — multiple solutions nested all the way down.
  W9  COMBAT IS OPTIONAL (mostly)
      persuade/sneak/teleport past fights — combat is ONE tool, and often not the best one; the systems let you AVOID it (validates a pacifist-capable spine).
  W10 MORALITY IS DISTRIBUTED ACROSS PATHS
      the mercy route (free Withermoore's soul), the justice route (clear Amyro), the tender route (reunite Migo/Yarrow), the brute route (kill everyone) — each escape is a different MORAL flavor, so HOW you leave characterizes you. ===============================================================================

### #16  THE NIGHTSONG / SHADOWHEART'S CHOICE (Baldur's Gate 3)
  W1  THE MACGUFFIN IS A PERSON
      hyped as a "relic" to hunt, revealed as a tortured prisoner — the treasure framing makes the moral reveal land harder (you came for loot, you found a soul).
  W2  THE CHOICE IS BOUND TO A COMPANION'S SOUL
      the fork isn't abstract — it decides who SHADOWHEART BECOMES (her faith, personality, romance, powers). Moral weight through a person you care about.
  W3  CHOICE READS THE WHOLE PLAYTHROUGH
      Shadowheart's lean is shaped by your cumulative good/evil acts — the game remembers everything and expresses it HERE (reactivity-as-memory at scale; cf. ME2 loyalty, Questbook 06).
  W4  THREE LEVELS OF CONSEQUENCE
      one choice hits the personal (romance), the companion (her arc), and the world (Shadow-Curse, Ketheric, Last Light Inn). Consequence stacked, not flat.
  W5  THE DUNGEON IS THE CHARACTER'S TEST
      the Gauntlet of Shar's trials ARE Shadowheart's faith dramatized (trust-the-invisible-bridge = a leap of faith) — staging that externalizes her inner conflict (cf. KCD's live-the-routine, Questbook 08).
  W6  DEFERRED REVEAL (long seeding)
      the "relic" is chased from Act 1 but only revealed in Act 2 — a mystery seeded for dozens of hours pays off with maximum weight.
  W7  THE RIVAL CLAIMANT
      Balthazar also wants the Nightsong -> a third party raises stakes + offers an alternative (hand her over) — the fork isn't just save/kill (cf. branch-router NPCs, Questbook 02).
  W8  NO CLEAN "CORRECT" (but consequences are real)
      the game supports evil (Dark Justiciar) as a full, rewarded path (powerful armor) — not a fail state; each path has gains AND losses (cf. NV/DOS2).
  W9  THE SOFT-TIMER ENVIRONMENT
      the Shadow-Curse pressures the approach (damage unless protected) — survival tension without a UI clock (cf. Questbooks 06/11).
  W10 ORDER/TIMING GATES CONSEQUENCE
      rushing a point-of-no-return LOCKS this content — the world moves on its own logic; when you act matters (cf. Whispering Hillock timing, Questbook 04).
  W11 THE SKILL-SHORTCUT
      a Perception check reveals a lever that BYPASSES the temple puzzle — build/ attention rewarded with a faster path (multiple keys; cf. Questbooks 02/03/15). ===============================================================================

### #17  THE FOUR-PILLAR MISSION + SOCIAL BOSS BATTLES (Deus Ex: Human Revolution / Mankind Divided)
  W1  EVERY SPACE, FOUR KEYS
      build every scenario so combat/stealth/hacking/social ALL reach the goal — the lock has four keys; players blend them. The choice is HOW you traverse, not a menu.
  W2  THE SOCIAL BOSS BATTLE
      make a CONVERSATION a winnable fight — read the opponent's psychology, pick tactics turn-by-turn, win or lose with no violence. Talking is a boss fight.
  W3  READ-THE-PERSON (partly randomized)
      responses shuffle so you must READ the individual, not memorize — the person is the puzzle (cf. Lady Boyle personality-deduction, Questbook 14).
  W4  THE ODDS-TILTER AUG (CASIE)
      an optional tool that reveals the psych profile + primes pheromones — tilts the check transparently (dress-for-the-check, Questbook 05); earnable with effort.
  W5  THE UNAIDED PEAK (Zeke Sanders)
      the most intense social battle gives NO assistance — your own read vs a sobbing hostage + a jittery gun. Removing the aid RAISES the tension and the reward.
  W6  PUBLIC-REPUTATION STAKES (Taggart on TV)
      a debate where winning DAMAGES the opponent's public image (he nearly cracks on air) — social consequence beyond the info you extract.
  W7  THE DEBATE-AS-CLIMAX (Darrow)
      out-argue a genius about the nature of mankind as a FINALE — the ultimate boss is a philosophical argument (cf. Planescape, Questbook 12).
  W8  FAILURE REROUTES (lose the talk -> take the vents)
      losing a social battle routes you to a stealth/traversal solution — failure is a branch, never a dead end (cf. Disco, Questbook 05).
  W9  DIEGETIC INFO IN THE SPACE
      keycodes on monitors, passwords in emails — the level teaches its own solution environmentally (cf. Vault 22, Questbook 03).
  W10 BUILD EXPRESSES YOU (with a breadth warning)
      your augs open routes; over-specializing corners you — options come from breadth. (And the honest flaw: don't make the climax betray the build promise.) ===============================================================================

### #18  KNOWLEDGE-AS-PROGRESSION (Outer Wilds)
  W1  KNOWLEDGE IS THE UPGRADE
      no gear/skills/keys — understanding is the ONLY progression; the PLAYER improves, not the avatar. The most intrinsic possible motivation (you want to KNOW).
  W2  EVERYTHING AVAILABLE FROM MINUTE ONE
      the whole world is open immediately; the only gate is comprehension. Non-linear by construction — the order is authored by the player's curiosity.
  W3  THE RUMOR WEB (curiosity as the quest log)
      a growing map of known-vs-implied that always gives a thread to pull, with NO waypoints — the player follows their own questions (cf. our unrecorded ledger as a living log).
  W4  "THERE IS ALWAYS A WAY" (the trust contract)
      every unreachable thing HAS a knowledge-key; the world never cheats. That reliability is what makes players keep exploring intrinsically.
  W5  KNOWLEDGE-GATES DISGUISED AS SKILL-GATES
      the hard zones yield to UNDERSTANDING (drift past the blind fish), not reflexes/gear — "I figured it out" beats "I leveled up."
  W6  THE CLOCKWORK WORLD
      the solar system changes through the loop; be at the right place at the right TIME — a self-directed living-clock (cf. Anju/Kafei, Questbook 11; ME2 clock, Questbook 06).
  W7  THE LOOP AS A UNIT OF LEARNING
      die/reset keeps only memory + log — failure costs nothing but time, and every loop banks knowledge. Death is a teacher, not a punishment (cf. Disco failure-as-content, Questbook 05; our succession fold).
  W8  THE PRESSURE IS GENEROUS
      the 22-min clock creates urgency without tyranny (generous fuel/oxygen) — a soft deadline that focuses without frustrating (the Anju-easing lesson, Questbook 11).
  W9  THE EMOTIONAL PAYOFF OF COMPREHENSION
      the finale lands because you UNDERSTAND — knowledge resolves into an emotional/philosophical acceptance (cf. Planescape's regret, Questbook 12; our Liberate).
  W10 UNREPLAYABLE BY DESIGN
      because progression IS knowledge, you can't un-know it — every discovery is genuinely once-only. The purity of the idea is also its poignancy. ===============================================================================

### #19  THE DEDUCTION ENGINE (Return of the Obra Dinn)
  W1  DEDUCTION IS THE GAMEPLAY
      observation + cross-reference + inference ARE the mechanics — no combat, no upgrades; the PLAYER's reasoning is the engine (cf. Outer Wilds knowledge-progression, Q18).
  W2  THE INVERTED MYSTERY
      face -> method -> name (you don't know who anyone IS) — flipping the detective structure creates a novel, deeper puzzle. Start from maximum ignorance.
  W3  THE HOLISTIC SCENE-READ
      the clue is rarely on the corpse — read the WHOLE tableau (who's near whom, ranks, clothing, absence) — every scene is a resource for identifying OTHERS. Look at everyone.
  W4  THE WITNESS-THE-INSTANT VERB (Memento Mortem)
      a single evocative verb (freeze + walk the moment of death) that's both narrative and mechanical — the mechanic IS the horror and the clue-source.
  W5  DEATH-CHAINING (memory within a memory)
      unreachable subjects become reachable by chaining from scenes where they appear — an elegant unlock structure that reveals the story in deducible order.
  W6  THE LOGIC-MESH (lateral information)
      most solutions need facts from OTHER scenes — the puzzle interlocks, so accrued knowledge cascades (solving one unlocks three). Cross-reference is the joy.
  W7  THE RULE OF THREE (validation without hand-holding)
      lock fates in sets of 3 — prevents blind brute-force AND lets a reasoned guess ride on two certainties. The system that makes a hard mystery FAIR and solvable. (The single most portable mechanic here.)
  W8  NO HARD FAIL, NO TIMER
      deduce at your leisure; "storm coming" just signals completeness — pressure- free thinking (cf. Outer Wilds' generous clock, Q18). Respect the player's pace.
  W9  THE DIFFICULTY EASES AT THE END
      3-correct drops to 2-correct near the finish — a hidden ramp that rewards progress and softens the tail (cf. Anju N64->3DS easing, Q11).
  W10 FULLY FAIR BY DESIGN (the contract)
      enough info to solve everything without guessing — AND the honest flaw: where the art/clue is ambiguous, the contract breaks. Fairness is non-negotiable for deduction games. ===============================================================================

### #20  THE GOLDEN RULE / TIME-LOOP MORALITY (The Forgotten City)
  W1  ONE RULE MAKES A SOCIETY
      a single high-concept law ("the many suffer for the sins of the one") turns a whole city into a moral pressure-cooker — every interaction is charged by the shared threat. A premise that generates endless situations from ONE idea.
  W2  THE UNDEFINED SIN (philosophy as gameplay)
      refusing to fix "sin" turns the city into a surveillance state and forces the player to reason about morality — the ambiguity IS the content (cf. no-clean- answer, Q03/Q04).
  W3  THE LOOP CARRIES KNOWLEDGE + INVENTORY
      re-sequence events with what you know/hold — solve later what was impossible earlier (cf. Outer Wilds Q18, Anju Q11); here YOU trigger the loop.
  W4  SINNING AS A TOOL (the dark exploit)
      you can break the Rule for gain and carry loot forward, dooming the (resettable) city — a morally-loaded systemic verb that reinvents "winning."
  W5  THE RED-HERRING PREMISE
      the stated task (find the culprit) is a deliberate misdirection that serves a hidden antagonist — the quest interrogates its OWN framing; the real mystery is deeper (cf. the MacGuffin-is-a-person twist, Q16).
  W6  BACKGROUND REACTIVITY (build opens world)
      your origin changes dialogue AND physical routes (fugitive speed -> unique geometry) — replayable, build-expressive exploration (cf. Deus Ex Q17, Disco Q05).
  W7  ESCALATING ENDINGS
      four endings from selfish-early to full-canon — engagement depth maps to outcome goodness; the best ending demands the most understanding + help (cf. Megaton divergence + ME2 preparation, Q06).
  W8  KNOWLEDGE COLLAPSES THE LOOPS
      the canon ending is reachable as early as loop 4 IF you know the path — mastery lets you skip the grind (cf. Anju two-loops Q11, Outer Wilds Q18). Knowing = speed.
  W9  THE ARGUE-THE-CREATOR CLIMAX
      end the horror by DEBATING its author with accumulated understanding — reason as the win condition (cf. Planescape Q12, Deus Ex Q17). Comprehension resolves the crisis.
  W10 PROVEN AS A MOD FIRST
      it began as a Skyrim quest mod (3M+ downloads) — the QUEST-CRAFT stood on its own before the graphics/engine. LESSON: a great quest is writing + structure, not production value. ===============================================================================

### #21  "YOU CAN'T SAVE EVERYONE" (Pathologic 2)
  W1  TIME AS A RESOURCE TO LOSE (not beat)
      the clock isn't a challenge to master — it's a scarcity to grieve; missing events/deaths is BUILT IN. The most distinctive time design in the medium.
  W2  "YOU CAN'T SAVE EVERYONE" AS THE THESIS
      inevitable loss is the CORE experience, not a fail state — the game mechanizes triage and grief; you play to manage failure, not avoid it.
  W3  THE SLOW-ONSET CRUELTY
      the pressure is absent early and creeps in by day 4-5 — you LEARN the cruelty by living it, so it lands as lived experience, not a rules-explanation.
  W4  THE BODY AS A SECOND CLOCK
      hunger/thirst/exhaustion/infection make mere survival cost time + resources — scarcity forces moral compromise (theft, hard bargains) organically.
  W5  TRIAGE AS THE CORE LOOP
      prioritize districts/people/factions with never enough — every save is a death elsewhere; the gameplay IS the ethics (cf. That Lucky Old Sun allocation, collection).
  W6  ODDS, NOT GUARANTEES
      treatment raises survival PROBABILITY, never certainty — you live with outcomes you influenced but didn't control (cf. ME2 survival math Q06). Uncertainty = weight.
  W7  THE DIEGETIC QUESTLOG (mindmap)
      the quest log IS the character's mind — story informs the very interface; tracking the plot is inhabiting the protagonist (cf. Obra Dinn Q19, Disco Q05).
  W8  THE NO-CLEAN FINALE (town vs magic)
      two reasonable, well-argued end-choices players genuinely flip on — and by the end "winning" is itself questionable (so few survive). Debate as the payoff.
  W9  THE METANARRATIVE FAIL-STATE
      miss the ending and the game breaks the fourth wall to berate you — form commenting on failure; the game is ABOUT its own unforgivingness.
  W10 SUFFERING AS DESIGN (+ the tuning-knob fix)
      the costs make the choices heavy — but it's alienating, so difficulty sliders let players set their own cruelty. Powerful + honest about its own hard sell. ===============================================================================

### #22  SIDE QUESTS AS PHILOSOPHICAL DESPAIR (NieR: Automata)
  W1  SIDE QUESTS DELIVER THE THEME (dark inverse of relief)
      the strong side quests DEEPEN the dread + the central question rather than relieving it — side content as a philosophy delivery system.
  W2  THE IMITATION ENGINE
      every side quest is a lifeform IMITATING humanity (love/family/faith/revenge) and it going wrong or bittersweet — one thematic engine generating endless micro-parables.
  W3  THE SIDE QUEST THAT DETONATES THE MAIN SECRET
      "Amnesia" quietly reveals the E-type executioner truth that reframes 2B & 9S's whole relationship — a "side" quest carrying a core revelation.
  W4  DRAMATIC IRONY VIA A SIDE BEAT
      "some things are better left unknown" lands because WE (may) know 2B's secret — the side quest weaponizes player knowledge against the characters.
  W5  HUMANIZING THE FUNCTIONAL
      the radio-operator "UI" characters get inner lives — even the interface is a person; nothing is just a system (cf. our unrecorded ledger's "everyone is someone").
  W6  RECONTEXT ACROSS PLAYTHROUGHS
      replaying as different characters REFRAMES the same events — perspective as progression; meaning changes, not difficulty (cf. loop-knowledge Q18/Q20).
  W7  NIHILISM -> CHOSEN MEANING (the arc)
      earn the despair (your war is a lie, everyone imitates a dead ideal), then transcend it — meaning is something we ASSIGN; hope after honesty (cf. Planescape's regret Q12, our Liberate "let go").
  W8  THE ATTENTIVE UNEARTH THE GRIEF
      recurring-character quests (Emil) reward the player who digs into long-buried loss (cf. foreshadow-in-hindsight Q10/Q11).
  W9  SYMPATHY FOR THE "ENEMY"
      side quests make you care about the machines you're told to kill — the designated enemy is humanized until killing feels wrong (cf. monster-is-a-victim, Bloody Baron Q01).
  W10 THE THEME IS A QUESTION, NOT A LECTURE
      "what is it to be human?" is asked through situations, never preached — the player arrives at the despair/hope themselves (cf. Planescape Q12, Forgotten City Q20). ===============================================================================

### #23  THE NO-MARKER QUESTLINE (Elden Ring / FromSoftware)
  W1  THE WORLD IS THE QUEST LOG
      no markers/log — quests live in dialogue, item text, and the environment; the PLAYER assembles them. Discovery is earned and personal (the anti-checklist).
  W2  THE QUIET THRILL OF STUMBLING ON THE NEXT STEP
      finding progression yourself (a re-visited NPC, a read description) is a discovery a waypoint would destroy — intrinsic-motivation gold.
  W3  ITEM DESCRIPTIONS AS LORE
      bury the deep story in flavor text the curious ASSEMBLE — narrative as an archaeological dig (cf. Obra Dinn Q19, Vault 22 Q03).
  W4  ENVIRONMENTAL STORYTELLING
      architecture/corpses/placement narrate history wordlessly — the space testifies (cf. the Bloody Baron's house Q01, Vault 22 Q03).
  W5  INTERLOCKING NPCs (early side = later thread)
      a character met on an unrelated early errand (Blaidd) turns out central to a major questline — quests WEAVE into one tapestry (cf. DOS2 Q15, KCD Q08).
  W6  NPCs PROGRESS INDEPENDENTLY
      characters live/move/die on world-time whether you watch or not — an alive, indifferent world (cf. NV pre-seeding, ME2/Anju clocks). Presence has stakes.
  W7  A SIDE QUEST THAT IS AN ENDING
      Ranni's questline yields a whole game ENDING + worldview — the ultimate "side content is the game" (cf. ME2 loyalty Q06, BG3 Nightsong Q16).
  W8  THE TRAGEDY SIGNATURE
      NPC quests mostly end sadly — a consistent melancholy that unifies the world's tone (cf. NieR Q22, Witcher Q01). Tonal coherence through recurring fate.
  W9  MAIN GATES SIDE (and vice versa)
      a MAIN boss (Radahn) gates a SIDE quest's key location (Nokron) — the main and side content interlock structurally, not just narratively.
  W10 THE FALSE BINARY REJECTED (the lesson from the CRITICISM)
      "reveal nothing vs reveal everything" is a false choice — the FIX is better in-world clues/dialogue/notes, NOT markers-or-nothing. Diegetic signposting is the craft. ===============================================================================

### #24  THE REACTIVITY ENGINE (Alpha Protocol)
  W1  REACTIVITY AS A WEB, NOT A BINARY
      track relationships + consequences across factions/people, not a good/evil bar — 32 endings from a web of small choices. The game REMEMBERS everything.
  W2  INTENT OVER SCRIPT (timed stances)
      pick an ATTITUDE under a clock, not exact words — models real-conversation pressure + commits you to a persona (cf. Deus Ex social battle Q17, Mass Effect wheel).
  W3  NO UNIVERSALLY-CORRECT CHOICE
      the stance that wins one NPC loses another — reputation is per-person and taste-based; you can't please everyone (cf. NV factions Q02, but per-individual).
  W4  LIKE vs RESPECT (multidimensional reputation)
      NPCs can respect you MORE for defying them — fear/ admiration/trust/resentment are distinct axes with distinct payoffs. Antagonism can be a valid, rewarded persona.
  W5  REPUTATION BUYS MECHANICS (incl
      combat): relationships re-tune the game — an ally poisons a boss's drugs; intel skips a mission. Consequence reaches into moment-to-moment MECHANICS, not just story.
  W6  BOSS-ALTERING CONSEQUENCE
      the deepest reactivity changes a BOSS FIGHT based on a past conversation — the narrative and mechanical layers fuse (a conversation three missions ago makes this fight easier).
  W7  INTEL AS SOCIAL POWER (dossiers)
      collecting info on an NPC UNLOCKS dialogue/leverage — knowing them is manipulating them (cf. CASIE Q17, Lady Boyle deduction Q14).
  W8  DELAYED, INVISIBLE-SEED CONSEQUENCE
      many choices only pay off hours later — the world has a long memory (cf. Whispering Hillock Q04, ME2 Q06, BG3 Q16).
  W9  PREP SHAPES OPTIONS
      vendor/intel prep before missions determines what's possible — preparation as a reactivity input (cf. ME2 wind-up Q06).
  W10 SURFACE THE CONSEQUENCE (the FLAW-fix)
      deep reactivity risks being unseen — ACKNOWLEDGE what the player did (an NPC references it, an ending tallies it) so it lands even on one playthrough. ===============================================================================

### #25  FAVOR & WRATH / PLAYING AFTER EVIL WON (Tyranny)
  W1  DUAL-AXIS REPUTATION (favor AND wrath, independent)
      not a good/evil slider — accumulate BOTH toward the same party; be respected AND resented at once. The definitive anti-morality-meter design.
  W2  FEAR IS AS POWERFUL AS LOVE
      high WRATH/FEAR unlocks its OWN abilities + unique bonuses — being feared is a mechanically rewarded path, not a penalty. Villainy/hardness is a real build.
  W3  FILTERED BY PRINCIPLE, NOT UNIVERSAL
      each faction judges acts by THEIR values — one act earns favor here and wrath there; there's no global "good." Relativism as a system (cf. Alpha Protocol Q24).
  W4  AUTHORITY AS THE FANTASY
      you start powerful (a Fatebinder/judge), not a nobody — the fantasy is WIELDING authority over the conquered, a fresh inversion of the ascent arc.
  W5  THE BANALITY OF EVIL
      most choices are the mundane administration of an unjust order (who governs, who's punished) — grey, everyday, historically real; more unsettling than cartoon villainy.
  W6  CHOICE BEFORE THE GAME (Conquest)
      a pre-game prologue shapes the STARTING world; NPCs reference decisions made before scene one — radical front-loaded reactivity (cf. Alpha Protocol delayed seeds Q24).
  W7  ALLEGIANCE REDRAWS THE MAP
      siding with a faction grants them territory/stewardship — reputation has GEOPOLITICAL, world-state consequences, not just dialogue (cf. NV factions Q02).
  W8  THE FORCED-BUT-OPEN ALLIANCE
      two opposite factions pull you to pick a side (or hold the middle) — mutually-exclusive allegiance with a hard third "stand above both" path (cf. NV's faction endgame).
  W9  COMPANIONS SERVE FROM LOVE OR FEAR (and it shows in the epilogue)
      loyalty/fear shapes their arcs + ending slides — HOW you earned their service defines their fate (cf. ME2 loyalty Q06, BG3 Q16).
  W10 THE FALSE-NEUTRAL PUPPETEER
      a faction claiming neutrality (preserve knowledge) is the real manipulator playing sides — the hidden hand (cf. the Network, our Amalgamation's Network handlers). ===============================================================================

### #26  THE UNSOLVABLE ACCUSATION (Pentiment)
  W1  THE UNSOLVABLE MYSTERY
      no true culprit, no confirmation — you act on belief under permanent uncertainty. Breaks the genre's fairness promise ON PURPOSE to say something about knowledge + blame.
  W2  NARRATIVE *ABOUT* INVESTIGATION
      the subject isn't "who did it" but "how we decide who did it, and what that costs" — the mechanic embodies the theme (epistemic humility, the weight of judgment).
  W3  TIME-TRIAGE ON KNOWLEDGE
      you can't chase every lead — where you SPEND time determines what you know, so the "culprit" is partly a function of your attention. Investigation as resource allocation (cf. Pathologic Q21).
  W4  EACH SUSPECT IS A QUESTLINE (with motive + weapon)
      guilt is built by digging a distinct thread per suspect — parallel cases you pick between (cf. Beyond the Beef's web Q02, Obra Dinn's mesh Q19).
  W5  ACCUSE-WHO-YOU-BELIEVE *OR* WHO-DESERVES-IT
      the fork separates TRUTH from JUSTICE — you can pursue the likely killer OR impart moral judgment on who deserves the gallows. Two different games of conscience (cf. Vault 22's moralize-the-lie Q03, Whispering Hillock's pure-ethics Q04).
  W6  YOU LIVE WITH BEING (MAYBE) WRONG
      the accused + their kin carry your choice for DECADES across acts — consequence you inhabit, not just trigger (cf. our fold; Whispering Hillock delayed payoff Q04).
  W7  MOTIVE AS THE HUNT (a goal inside chaos)
      centering MOTIVE gives a clear objective + a pass/fail inside an unsolvable frame — structure that keeps an open mystery playable (not just vibes).
  W8  BUILD DEFINES WHAT YOU CAN KNOW
      Andreas' self-defined background gates which clues he reads — who you ARE shapes what you can PERCEIVE (cf. Disco Q05, Deus Ex Q17, Forgotten City backgrounds Q20).
  W9  HISTORY AS THE REAL SUBJECT
      the mystery is a lens on class/faith/power + how official "truth" gets authored by the strong — the quest carries a real-world meditation (cf. our life-lesson-under-every- decision rule; the recorded-vs-unrecorded theme).
  W10 THE DECADES-LONG AFTERMATH
      returning across 25 years to see judgments ripen — the game makes you INHABIT the long tail of your uncertainty (near-identical to our generational structure). ===============================================================================

### #27  THE ILLUSION OF CHOICE / PLAYER COMPLICITY (Spec Ops: The Line)
  W1  THE GENRE-TRAP
      wear the skin of a familiar power fantasy, then deconstruct it from inside — the player's expectations become the ammunition (cf. Undertale-style subversion; NieR Q22).
  W2  STRIP THE CHOICE, FORCE THE HAND
      remove moral agency (scripted order) but make the player EXECUTE the act (aim + fire) — complicity WITHOUT decision; you did it even though you couldn't choose not to.
  W3  WEAPONIZE THE ABSTRACTION
      use the interface conventions players never question (dots on a screen, "neutralize") then reveal their human cost — the UI itself is the lie.
  W4  THE ACCUSATORY UI
      turn the game's own helper-text (loading tips) into second-person accusation — the system addresses the PLAYER, not the character. Chilling, cheap (in a good way), unforgettable.
  W5  SYMPATHY-THEN-SLAUGHTER
      engineer connection, then force harm — guilt built on prior empathy (cf. Q01/Q22). The player mourns what they destroyed.
  W6  THE UNRELIABLE, SELF-DECEIVING HERO
      the protagonist invents a villain + rewrites reality to dodge guilt — a study in how atrocity gets denied (cf. Dream On's implicated investigator Q09).
  W7  NAME THE PLAYER'S MOTIVE
      "you wanted to feel like a hero" — indict the fantasy the player came FOR. The game knows why you're playing and holds it up.
  W8  THE VISIBLE DEGRADATION
      Walker's body/voice/uniform rot as he descends — external state mirrors moral collapse (cf. our character-degradation art potential; show the cost).
  W9  FORM = INDICTMENT
      the critique IS the experience (you don't watch atrocity, you commit it) — the strongest version of theme-through-mechanic (cf. Dead Money greed, collection; Pathologic Q21).
  W10 THE HONEST LIMIT
      forcing the player through the condemned act risks tedium/preachiness — the lesson is to make complicity MEANINGFUL + earned, not a hectoring gotcha (our care + tone rules). ===============================================================================

### #28  MERCY AS A MECHANIC (Undertale)
  W1  MERCY AS A FULL MECHANIC
      sparing is a real combat SYSTEM (ACT->calm->SPARE), not a stealth-bypass — non-violence has its own puzzles + skill (dodge while you solve). Pacifism is GAMEPLAY, not evasion.
  W2  EVERY ENEMY IS A PERSON WITH A SOLUTION
      each foe has a name, personality, + a specific non-violent ACT — killing has weight because nothing is a faceless mob (cf. NieR Q22, Undertale-humanizes-all).
  W3  READING WHO THEY ARE = THE SOLUTION
      pacifying an enemy means understanding them (comfort the lonely, encourage the shy) — characterization IS the mechanic (cf. Deus Ex Q17, Whodunit Q07).
  W4  THE PERSISTENT, UNFORGETTING SAVE
      an irreversible moral choice that STICKS beyond resets — the world remembers your worst act forever; you can't launder it by reloading. The ultimate "world remembers."
  W5  THE WORLD DECAYS WITH YOUR CRUELTY
      music/NPCs/atmosphere physically reflect your body count (empty towns, eerie tunes) — HOW you play reshapes the WORLD-STATE (cf. Spec Ops Q27, Dishonored chaos Q14).
  W6  MERCY IS EARNED, NOT PASSIVE
      the game NUDGES you to kill (escalating bosses, "kill me" pleas) — true pacifism requires REFUSING every easy violent out. Non-violence as active discipline (cf. Q14).
  W7  THE ROUTE IS THE THEME
      three routes = three moral stances; how you treat the world IS the story + the ending. Play-style as narrative (cf. Tyranny Q25, our Liberate/Respect/Become).
  W8  META-COMMENTARY ON WHY
      it interrogates the PLAYER'S motive ("you did it just to see") — curiosity- as-cruelty; the game asks why you were WILLING (the bright twin of Spec Ops Q27).
  W9  THE BRIGHT COUNTERWEIGHT
      unlike Spec Ops (forces atrocity), Undertale OFFERS a fully-realized non-violent path AND a violent one — the player CHOOSES, so the meaning is truly theirs (validates our Pacifist Path Law: always offer the real non-lethal route).
  W10 SPARING STILL TAKES SKILL
      you dodge a bullet-hell while solving the enemy — mercy isn't the EASY button; it's a different, equally-demanding challenge. Non-violence with teeth. ===============================================================================

### #29  THE BOOK OF LAWS / SOCIETY-SURVIVAL (Frostpunk)
  W1  GOVERNANCE IS THE QUEST
      running a society under scarcity IS the gameplay — resource management fused with moral law-making; every system asks a values question. (The city-builder AS an ethics engine.)
  W2  THE BOOK OF LAWS (one law/day)
      a paced cadence of committed, branching, mutually-exclusive laws — slow enough that each is FELT; society changes one deliberate step at a time.
  W3  THE SLIPPERY SLOPE
      each reasonable law greases the next; no single choice is monstrous but the CUMULATIVE drift is — the horror of gradualism (prison -> re-education -> propaganda -> labor camp).
  W4  THE EMBLEMATIC COMPROMISE (child labor)
      one vivid slider between expedience and decency the game never pretends is free — a concrete moral image, not an abstract policy.
  W5  DUAL SOCIETY METERS (hope vs discontent)
      keep everyone ALIVE and still be OVERTHROWN for HOW — two simultaneous failure axes (physical survival vs political legitimacy).
  W6  "THE CITY MUST SURVIVE" -> "WHO DID YOU BECOME"
      the ending judges the RAMIFICATIONS OF HOW you survived, not whether — survival is the premise, character is the verdict (cf. Frostpunk's "crossed the line" finale; our Liberate/Respect/Become).
  W7  THEME THROUGH SYSTEMS
      you MAKE hard choices under a ticking thermometer, never read about them — the mechanics carry the ethics (cf. Pathologic Q21, Spec Ops Q27, Dead Money).
  W8  IDEOLOGICAL FORKS (order vs faith)
      mutually-exclusive ways to manufacture hope + suppress dissent — the SAME goal (social control) via opposite value systems; your pick defines the regime (cf. Tyranny Disfavored/Chorus Q25).
  W9  THE QUIET JUDGMENT (you don't have to)
      the dark laws are OPTIONAL and the ending implies you shouldn't — no explicit "correct," but your drift is tallied (cf. the unrecorded ledger).
  W10 LEGITIMACY AS A FAIL-STATE
      you can be EXILED for losing the people even while physically surviving — a distinct political failure mode (cf. our mayor-consequence + succession). ===============================================================================

### #30  THE CIVILIAN PERSPECTIVE / GUILT AS A SYSTEM (This War of Mine)
  W1  THE PERSPECTIVE INVERSION (victims, not soldiers)
      re-center catastrophe on the POWERLESS — the emotional engine of the whole game; you defend family, not conquer (cf. our post-collapse survivors).
  W2  GUILT AS A MECHANIC
      survivors have MENTAL health that cruelty erodes (sad -> broken -> suicide/ catatonia) and kindness lifts — conscience is a managed resource; the psychological cost is SYSTEMIZED.
  W3  GREY MORALITY, NO RIGHT ANSWER
      altruism costs survival, cruelty costs the soul — every choice is a real trade with no clean option (cf. Pathologic Q21, Pentiment Q26, Whispering Hillock Q04).
  W4  THE EMBLEMATIC DILEMMA (the Quiet House)
      one concrete, unforgettable moral image (rob the scared, unarmed, sick elderly couple) — a vivid scene, not an abstract policy (cf. Frostpunk child-labor Q29).
  W5  BUILD THE SYSTEM AROUND EMERGENT EMOTION
      the guilt mechanic exists because a playtester felt guilt unprompted (returned to un-steal) — WATCH for emergent player feeling and mechanize it. (A profound design method: let players teach you what the game is about.)
  W6  THE SUBTRACTIVE/MIRROR EXPERIENCE
      withhold guidance so players draw their OWN conclusions, then mirror choices back as discomfort — discomfort WITHOUT forcing it (the ethical improvement on Spec Ops Q27; you always choose, so the guilt is truly yours — cf. Undertale Q28).
  W7  NO ONBOARDING + PERMADEATH
      learn-by-failing disorientation + irreversible loss simulate war's precariousness (cf. Pathologic Q21, Undertale Q28, our fold).
  W8  COMMUNITY AS A SURVIVAL RESOURCE
      survivors telling stories / caring for each other MITIGATES trauma — social bonds are mechanically load-bearing (cf. our companion systems; the anti-isolation).
  W9  ATTRITION CASCADES
      small neglect snowballs (overexertion->sickness->depression->dysfunction) — the death spiral makes early kindness/harshness compound (cf. Frostpunk Q29). Consequences interlock.
  W10 THE PACIFIST RUN IS POSSIBLE
      you CAN survive as "mister nice guy," never stealing/killing — mercy is a viable (harder) path, always your choice (validates our Pacifist Path Law; cf. Undertale Q28). ===============================================================================

### #31  THE IRON CAGE / COMPLICITY AS A JOB (Papers, Please)
  W1  COMPLICITY THROUGH MUNDANE WORK
      you administer cruelty via BORING paperwork — the banality is the horror; you're an accomplice one stamp at a time (cf. Tyranny Q25, Spec Ops Q27 — the paperwork version).
  W2  THE IRON CAGE (felt monotony)
      the game replicates bureaucratic tedium to TRAP you in a rule-following system that replaces judgment — you FEEL the cage (timer/quota/rulebook). Form = the theme.
  W3  SCARCITY WEAPONIZES COMPASSION AGAINST YOUR OWN
      mercy risks a citation that STARVES YOUR FAMILY — the cruelest vise; kindness to a stranger endangers your child. Survival vs conscience, made personal.
  W4  THE ESCALATING RULEBOOK
      complexity piles up daily until keeping up is frantic — the SYSTEM'S growth is the difficulty curve; you err under load (cf. Frostpunk escalating laws Q29).
  W5  DETAIN = CRUELTY INCENTIVIZED
      the regime PAYS you to hand over the desperate — the systems reward the immoral choice, so virtue has a price tag (cf. Dishonored's dark spare Q14, Whodunit bonus Q07 inverted).
  W6  RECURRING HUMAN FACES
      applicants' stories RETURN (the wife following her husband) — the rules become personal; enforcing them separates families you've met (cf. Anju/Kafei Q11, monster-is-a-victim Q01).
  W7  SUBVERT THE CAGE (EZIC)
      you can SABOTAGE the regime from inside your booth at grave risk — cog OR saboteur; complicity is a choice you can refuse (cf. get-caught-on-purpose Q15, villain-route Q02).
  W8  MANY SMALL WEIGHTED CHOICES > ONE BIG TREE
      depth from the ACCUMULATION of tiny pressured decisions, not a branching dialogue tree — a different, valid moral-design model (cf. our death-math cadence).
  W9  ~20 ENDINGS FROM THE DRIFT
      accumulated choices branch to divergent fates (jail/execution/escape/ revolution) — the sum of small acts is your ending (cf. Alpha Protocol Q24, Frostpunk Q29, Megaton).
  W10 THEME THROUGH THE INTERFACE
      the rulebook, stamp, and booth ARE the argument — you don't read about bureaucracy, you DO it (cf. Pathologic mindmap Q21, Obra Dinn logbook Q19 — same designer). ===============================================================================

### #32  "YOU ARE THE VILLAIN" / THE IDENTITY TWIST (KOTOR)
  W1  THE TWIST THAT REWRITES THE PAST
      the reveal retroactively recontextualizes every prior scene WITHOUT changing a frame — the whole game reorganizes in your head. Maximum payoff from prior content.
  W2  YOU ARE THE VILLAIN YOU HUNTED (the ultimate mirror)
      you've been chasing yourself — identity as the final antagonist (cf. Baron Q01, Planescape Q12, RDR Q10). The mirror taken to its literal extreme.
  W3  THE TWIST IS A CHOICE, NOT JUST A SHOCK
      post-reveal AGENCY — redeem or relapse; the player AUTHORS who they now are (the RPG advantage over film twists; cf. Planescape "change the nature of a man" Q12).
  W4  FAIR-PLAY SEEDING
      clued relentlessly (Force aptitude, languages, false-memory cracks, NPC reactions) so it's inevitable-in-hindsight, not cheap — the fairness contract (cf. Obra Dinn Q19).
  W5  DELIVERED AT THE LOWEST POINT, BY THE ENEMY
      staged when you're captured + broken, from your foe, weaponized to shatter you — maximum emotional impact (cf. Peralez Q09, the Tribunal Q05).
  W6  THE TWIST TESTS YOUR BONDS
      it detonates the PARTY (Carth's grief, Bastila's guilt) — every relationship reframed; companions react per their history (cf. ME2 Q06, BG3 Q16, Alpha Protocol Q24).
  W7  RETROACTIVE + PROSPECTIVE STAKES
      it reframes the PAST and raises the stakes of the FUTURE (your choices now decide if a war criminal stays redeemed) — the twist works in both directions.
  W8  IDENTITY AS THE THEME
      "are you who you WERE or who you CHOOSE to be?" — the twist IS the game's thesis, not a gimmick (cf. Planescape Q12, our succession/upbringing).
  W9  ONE-SHOT RESOURCE, SO BUILD AROUND IT
      the magic is spent on first play — the surrounding RPG must stand alone (cf. Alpha Protocol's replay model Q24 as the contrast). Spend the twist wisely.
  W10 MOTIVATED AMNESIA
      memory-loss works because it's justified (the Jedi's plan) + clued + thematically load-bearing — not a lazy blank slate (cf. Planescape memory-as-identity Q12). ===============================================================================

### #33  "WOULD YOU KINDLY" / THE AGENCY TWIST (BioShock)
  W1  THE TWIST INDICTS THE PLAYER'S OBEDIENCE
      not just the character — YOU did everything the game said, unquestioning; "would you kindly" was aimed at you. Metacommentary on how players play (cf. Spec Ops Q27).
  W2  LINEARITY BECOMES THE THEME
      the medium's constraint (locked doors, one path) IS the mind control — a limitation reframed as meaning. Weaponize your own structure (the masterstroke).
  W3  THE TRIGGER HIDDEN IN PLAIN SIGHT
      the clue ("would you kindly") is audible from minute one but disguised as a verbal tic — invisible until named, chilling on replay (fairness via ubiquity; cf. Q32/Q19).
  W4  DEMONSTRATED, NOT TOLD (the mechanical proof)
      after the reveal the game LOCKS your agency so you FEEL the control — the mechanic proves the theme (cf. Spec Ops Q27, theme-through-mechanic Q21).
  W5  THE FALSE GUIDE
      the trusted helper-voice is the villain — betray the most basic dependence (needing a guide in an unknown world) (cf. Peralez Q09, false-neutral Q25, Papers' EZIC Q31).
  W6  THEME + TWIST FUSED (Objectivist irony)
      the city of "free will" made a perfect slave — the reveal IS the philosophical argument, not decoration (cf. Planescape Q12, KOTOR Q32).
  W7  "A MAN CHOOSES, A SLAVE OBEYS"
      one line crystallizes the whole theme + accuses the player — economy of meaning (cf. RDR "many have" Q10, the single perfect line).
  W8  AGENCY RESTORED THEN TESTED
      post-reveal, real choice returns (save/harvest) and the ending hinges on it — now that you CAN choose, what do you do? (cf. KOTOR redeem/relapse Q32, Undertale Q28).
  W9  THE FRIENDLY-VOICE DEPENDENCE
      it works because you genuinely NEEDED Atlas to navigate — the twist exploits a real player need, not a contrivance (cf. our companion/guide systems).
  W10 THE HONEST LIMIT
      critiquing linearity while staying linear is hypocritical; a reveal that doesn't change GAMEPLAY sags — pair the narrative twist with a mechanical shift (our lesson to do better). ===============================================================================

### #34  THE COIN TOSS IS A LIE / CONSCIOUSNESS-COPY HORROR (SOMA)
  W1  HORROR FROM AN IDEA, NOT A MONSTER
      the terror is a QUESTION about the self (is the copy you?) — metaphysical dread outlasts any jump-scare (cf. Dream On epistemic horror Q09). Ideas haunt longest.
  W2  THE COMFORTING LIE (the coin toss)
      a false 50/50 "transfer" that preserves the fantasy of continuity — people CLING to it because the truth (you're just left behind) is unbearable. A lie the player wants to believe (cf. Spec Ops self-deception Q27, atrocity-denial).
  W3  POV AS THE ARGUMENT
      the game moves the player's viewpoint between copies so YOU live the illusion, making its collapse personal — the mechanic teaches the philosophy (cf. BioShock Q33, theme-through- mechanic Q21).
  W4  THE ABANDONED SELF (show, don't tell)
      stage the truth by leaving a version of you awake + screaming that he didn't make it — the horror is DEMONSTRATED, unavoidable, not argued (the fix for idea-horror).
  W5  THE STRUCTURALLY-HONEST ENDING
      the ending wounds because it REFUSES the fantasy — the copy is happy, YOU are left behind; it earns its devastation by being true to its own premise (cf. Dream On non- ending Q09, Pathologic Q21). Honesty over comfort.
  W6  MORAL TRIAGE FROM CONTINUITY
      once a copy deserves moral consideration, every "moving on" is abandonment or murder — "someone always keeps the suffering." No clean choice (cf. Pathologic Q21, TWoM Q30, Whispering Hillock Q04).
  W7  THE FALSE SALVATION (the ARK)
      a "digital afterlife" that generates SUCCESSORS, not survival — comfort for copies, abandonment for originals; "grief rewritten by engineers who never solved grief."
  W8  THE LIE IS MOTIVATED
      Catherine withholds the truth because she NEEDS Simon compliant — the deception is character-driven, not authorial (cf. KOTOR Q32). Make manufactured hope motivated.
  W9  TUNE-DOWN THE WEAK LAYER
      a "safe mode" lets players focus on the theme over the stealth — when the idea is the strength, let players lower the action (cf. Pathologic sliders Q21, our packages).
  W10 IT HAUNTS FOR YEARS (the mark of idea-horror)
      players "re-think it for hours/years after" — the sign that theme-through-experience worked. Aim for the question that won't leave them. ===============================================================================

### #35  THE TOWN AS PSYCHE / GUILT MADE LEVEL DESIGN (Silent Hill 2)
  W1  THE WORLD IS THE PSYCHE
      the town/fog/monsters/layout ARE the protagonist's inner life — you explore a MIND, not a place; every element means something about the character (cf. Q23/Q03, interiorized).
  W2  THE UNRELIABLE PROTAGONIST (slow-drip truth)
      James's contradictions (Mary dead 3 years / just wrote him) seed a repressed truth the game slowly cracks — the story is a psyche staging its own trial (cf. Spec Ops Q27, SOMA Q34).
  W3  MONSTERS AS SYMBOLIC SELF
      each creature encodes a specific guilt/repression (confinement, desire, punishment) — enemy design AS characterization; the horror is the protagonist (cf. NieR imitation Q22).
  W4  THE SELF-PUNISHMENT ENGINE (Pyramid Head)
      a monster you CAN'T defeat until you're ready to face the truth — you created your own executioner; catharsis is gated on ACCEPTANCE, not violence.
  W5  THE FADING OBJECT (diegetic unreliability)
      the letter's text fades to nothing as the delusion cracks — a physical, in-world tell; SHOW the unreliability (cf. SOMA's abandoned self Q34, Obra Dinn Q19).
  W6  PERSONALIZED HELLS (per-character manifestation)
      each visitor sees a town shaped by THEIR guilt — the same place, different interiors; a system for symbolic worlds (cf. Forgotten City per-person sin Q20).
  W7  THE ENDING IS EARNED BY BEHAVIOR, NOT CHOSEN
      subtle playstyle (how you treat Mary's items, whether you play "suicidally") reads James's self-judgment and hands him the verdict — the subconscious as input (cf. ME2 prep Q06, Undertale route Q28, BG3 cumulative lean Q16).
  W8  THE ENDING IS SELF-JUDGMENT
      forgive / condemn / repeat / deny — the four endings are four verdicts James passes on himself; the theme (can you forgive yourself?) IS the choice (cf. Planescape Q12, our Liberate/Respect/Become).
  W9  GRIEF + GUILT AS THE ENGINE (not gore)
      the true horror is emotional (killed his suffering wife, can't face it) — psychological, not splatter; it haunts because it's HUMAN (cf. SOMA Q34, Bloody Baron Q01).
  W10 SYMBOLISM LAYERED FOR SURFACE + DEPTH
      works as dread even undecoded, AND rewards analysis — meaning that doesn't REQUIRE the wiki but deepens with it (the fix for opacity; cf. Elden Ring Q23). ===============================================================================

### #36  THE BETRAYING GUIDE-VOICE (Portal / GLaDOS)
  W1  A VOICE AS A WHOLE CHARACTER
      a disembodied AI narrator becomes an all-time villain through DIALOGUE + DELIVERY + timing alone — great antagonists can be pure voice-writing (cf. our networked Amalgamation).
  W2  THE GUIDE WHO TURNS
      the trusted tutorial voice becomes the enemy — betray the most basic trust (the one teaching you the game); it cuts deep BECAUSE you needed her (cf. BioShock Q33, Peralez Q09).
  W3  COMEDY AS A DELIVERY SYSTEM FOR DREAD
      humor disarms + endears, making the menace underneath hit harder — funny and frightening in one breath (cf. Yakuza Q13, weaponized for a villain).
  W4  THE GRADUAL ESCALATION
      helpful -> passive-aggressive -> murderous, so slowly you can't name the turn — a relationship curdling in real time (cf. slow-onset dread Pathologic Q21).
  W5  THE FALSE REWARD (operant conditioning)
      a promised reward (cake) drives compliance without delivery; doubting it collapses control — obedience runs on a lie the player unlearns (cf. SOMA Q34, false-dawn Q048).
  W6  DOUBLE UNRELIABILITY (distrust becomes correct)
      she lies about the promise AND the denial — you can't trust either; skepticism is the winning stance (cf. Pentiment Q26).
  W7  MANUFACTURED ATTACHMENT, THEN FORCED BETRAYAL (Companion Cube)
      engineer love specifically to make its destruction hurt + test obedience — emotional manipulation as a designed mechanic (cf. Spec Ops Q27).
  W8  UNRELIABLE NARRATOR AS A MECHANIC
      her lies are GAMEPLAY (false instructions, misleading warnings) — learning to DISOBEY the narrator is the progression (cf. BioShock's obey-twist Q33, inverted).
  W9  THE MEMORABLE VILLAIN LINE
